\n</div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sat, 17 Oct 2020 08:00:00 +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/15/Become-a-Bartender-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-1-Version-2.jpg","linkMd5":"b2502d810ecdfe065551cdc1d9bd3c75","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn9@2020_6/2020/10/18/17-02-02-609_d4b95a9cc6609174.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":546,"sourceBytes":65169,"destBytes":47204,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/15/Become-a-Bartender-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-1-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn9@2020_6/2020/10/18/17-02-02-609_d4b95a9cc6609174.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e1/Become-a-Bartender-Step-2.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn92@2020_1/2020/10/18/17-02-17-155_909c0c1f562907ae.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b4/Become-a-Bartender-Step-3-Version-2.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-3-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn55@2020_3/2020/10/18/17-02-16-131_7f14b0cd7aa3635a.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a8/Become-a-Bartender-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-4-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn12@2020_4/2020/10/18/17-02-17-466_580569ad5d16eff9.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e2/Become-a-Bartender-Step-05.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-05.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn72@2020_4/2020/10/18/17-02-16-241_aaad390515f8d45f.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fc/Become-a-Bartender-Step-06.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-06.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn55@2020_5/2020/10/18/17-02-16-142_a63ab877b786d99a.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c6/Become-a-Bartender-Step-7-Version-2.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-7-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn31@2020_1/2020/10/18/17-02-16-230_0bd14cbb74ae9bf7.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/85/Become-a-Bartender-Step-8.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-8.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn44@2020_5/2020/10/18/17-02-16-139_f5c969322cb7582a.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/54/Become-a-Bartender-Step-9.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn72@2020_4/2020/10/18/17-02-17-219_bf9de6379c7e361f.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c1/Become-a-Bartender-Step-10.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn88@2020_2/2020/10/18/17-02-17-054_4f83f581a0900dde.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e4/Become-a-Bartender-Step-11.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn76@2020_6/2020/10/18/17-02-17-320_5f11519f6fc4398a.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/45/Become-a-Bartender-Step-12.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn38@2020_6/2020/10/18/17-02-16-099_a9531954c3fb0353.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9d/Become-a-Bartender-Step-13.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-13.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn63@2020_1/2020/10/18/17-02-17-199_813633e192feec2f.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a0/Become-a-Bartender-Step-14.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-14.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn23@2020_1/2020/10/18/17-02-16-175_87fad344d08d7251.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c5/Become-a-Bartender-Step-15.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-15.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn47@2020_1/2020/10/18/17-02-16-229_5f1b4e74d2dd1682.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8b/Become-a-Bartender-Step-16.jpg/aid2697745-v4-728px-Become-a-Bartender-Step-16.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn68@2020_3/2020/10/18/17-02-16-110_bd3fc2a3cca6eeb6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603040522099},{"createdTime":"2020-10-19 01:02:02","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 01:02:02","title":"How to Hang Pictures","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Pictures can add a lot of character and personality to your room, and can really tie a living space together. The possibilities for displaying some of your favorite pictures and paintings may seem endless, but there are several ways to make the process a little bit easier. You don’t need a lot of home decorating experience to hang up your pictures—all you need are a few measurements and the proper hanging hardware to take your decor to the next level. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Hang-Pictures&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Hang-Pictures&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Arranging Your Pictures with Templates\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Arranging-Your-Pictures-with-Templates\">Arranging Your Pictures with Templates</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Mark from the floor onto your wall. Grab a metal measuring tape and hold it in place along the baseboards, or where the floor meets the wall. Extend the tape until it reads about , which equals the average person’s eye level. Pencil over the wall with this measurement, so you have an idea of where your pictures need to go.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-1-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 1 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ab/Hang-Pictures-Step-1-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-1-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If your pictures are too high or too low, they may set the room a little off-balance. It’ll also be difficult for visitors to view and appreciate the art.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Organize your pictures by color. Find a common color theme that ties some of your pictures together. Before you start laying out your design, think about which pictures will look best together. Your room will look more seamless if you decorate it with similar, cohesive pictures.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-2-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 2 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e9/Hang-Pictures-Step-2-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-2-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For instance, you can hang up a group of black-and-white family pictures, or choose several pictures that have a splash of green or yellow.</li> \n    <li>You may also want to decorate with groups of similar pictures, like family portraits.</li> \n    <li>Consider choosing similar frames, prints, or other mounting choices for your pictures so they all look uniform.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Find-a-Stud\" title=\"Find a Stud\">Locate a wall stud</a> with a stud finder if you’re displaying heavy pictures. Hold your stud finder so it’s flush against the wall. Turn on the device and move it in a slow, horizontal motion. Wait for the stud finder to blink or beep, which lets you know where the stud is. Mark this spot with a pencil, so you know where a heavy picture should go.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-3-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 3 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/78/Hang-Pictures-Step-3-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-3-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re hanging multiple heavy pictures, double-check that they’re all centered over a wall stud.</li> \n    <li>A heavy picture is considered or more.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>You can pick up a stud finder online, or at your local hardware or home improvement store.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Create paper templates to help you lay out your pictures. Place your pictures on a large sheet of newsprint or craft paper. Trace around the perimeter of each picture, then cut out each individual template. Measure and cut out templates for all the pictures you plan on displaying, so you can get an idea of how they’ll look grouped together. As you cut out each template, label it so you can remember the picture it corresponds with.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-4-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 4 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d2/Hang-Pictures-Step-4-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-4-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Try to make these templates as exact as possible so you have a really clear idea of how your actual pictures will look once they’re displayed.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Secure the templates to your wall with painter’s tape. Arrange each piece of paper on the wall 1 at a time, so you can get an idea of how the finished display will look. Center the templates on the wall until you’re happy with their placement. At this point, you can take 4 pieces of painter’s tape and stick them to the corners of each template.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-5-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 5 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/11/Hang-Pictures-Step-5-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-5-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Depending on how many pictures you’re displaying, this process may be a little time consuming.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Center the group of templates over the previous mark you made. View your templates as parts of a whole instead of individual pictures. Try to center the entire group of templates on top of the eye-level marking you made previously. Take as much time as you need to tweak and adjust each individual template until the templates look centered.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-6-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 6 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e2/Hang-Pictures-Step-6-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-6-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Your largest template will likely be covering the eye-level marking.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Experiment by placing your templates in different arrangements. Play around with the templates until you find a grouping that you really like. You may prefer to place your largest template in the center, and display the smaller templates around the outside of the frame. If your pictures are all the same size, you may enjoy hanging your templates in a row or column.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-7-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 7 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a9/Hang-Pictures-Step-7-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-7-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>It may help to organize your templates on your floor before transferring them to the wall. This way, you can get a better idea of how certain pictures look next to one another.</li> \n    <li>For instance, if you’re working with a smaller section of wall, you can hang the templates in a column.</li> \n    <li>If you’re arranging pictures above furniture, like a sofa, leave of space between the top of the couch and the bottom of the lowest painting. If you’re displaying art over a table, leave of space.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>Space multiple pictures out evenly.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Measure the top of your templates with a level. Hold a level along the top edge of each template. Double-check that each piece of paper is completely straight. If a template seems off-kilter, remove the tape and lightly adjust the paper until the level gives a completely straight reading.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-8-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 8 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/5f/Hang-Pictures-Step-8-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-8-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This may seem a bit tedious, but helps ensure that your pictures will look even once they’re displayed on the wall.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Mark the top center point of the template along the wall. Stretch a tape measure along the top edge of each paper template. Find the exact center point on this edge, and mark it with a pencil. Repeat this process with all of the templates, then remove them from the wall.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-9-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 9 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/03/Hang-Pictures-Step-9-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-9-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Most pictures will have measurements that are easy to divide in half, like .</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Hang-Pictures&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Choosing the Proper Hardware\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Choosing-the-Proper-Hardware\">Choosing the Proper Hardware</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Test your wall with a pin to see if it’s drywall or something harder. Find an open area of wall and stick a thumbtack into the surface. If the thumbtack goes in, you can assume that your wall is made with drywall. If the tack won’t go in, it's possible (though not certain) that your wall is made with masonry, concrete, or another hard substance.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-10-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 10 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/87/Hang-Pictures-Step-10-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-10-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can disregard this if you already know what kind of wall you have.</li> \n    <li>Some wall hardware is better-suited to specific wall types. For instance, self-tapping anchors and D-rings work best with drywall.</li> \n    <li>For harder surfaces, like brick, you can use brick hangers or brick clips.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pick out adhesive hanging strips for a simple option on any wall. Visit your local general or hardware store to find adhesive strips, which you can stick to the back of your pictures. These strips are very easy to use, though they may not be the best option for heavier pieces of art. Before hanging anything up, always double-check the weight specifications on the product label.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-11-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 11 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/96/Hang-Pictures-Step-11-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-11-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can find adhesive strips online, or at a variety of different stores.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Display pictures with a D-ring if you’re drilling into a soft surface. Look for D-rings at your local hardware or home improvement store, which make it easy to hang up your pictures. Attach the hardware along the backside of your picture frame with a screw, which will support your picture and make it easy to display on the wall. Screw the D-ring hooks directly into the wall with an electric drill, which will support and hold up the D-rings along the back of the picture.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-12-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 12 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0b/Hang-Pictures-Step-12-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-12-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>As the name suggests, D-rings have a curved hook that helps secure the picture to the wall.</li> \n    <li>D-rings work best with a drillable surface, like drywall.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Opt for self-tapping anchors if you’re working with drywall. Insert a Philip’s screwdriver along the base of the anchor and screw it into the drywall. Once the anchor is securely embedded in the wall, screw a metal hook into the opening. You can use these anchors, screws and hooks to display pictures that weigh up to .<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-13-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 13 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/dd/Hang-Pictures-Step-13-Version-4.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-13-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can purchase these anchors online, or at most hardware or home improvement shops.</li> \n    <li>Double-check the weight limit listed on the product label before hanging up any pictures.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Hang up heavier items with toggle bolts. Slide a nut and 1-2 washers onto 1 end of the toggle bolt, then slide the spring-loaded metal wings onto 1 end.<sup id=\"_ref-19\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 19\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-19\">[19]</a></sup> Drill a hole into your wall, then press the metal “wings” down along both sides of the bolt. Insert the bolt into the hole—once it’s in the wall, the wings will extend, providing more support. Screw a hook or other hanging attachment to the opposite end of the toggle bolt, which will support your picture.<sup id=\"_ref-20\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 20\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-20\">[20]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-14-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 14 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6d/Hang-Pictures-Step-14-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-14-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can center really heavy pictures over this bolt, which will help keep them steady.<sup id=\"_ref-21\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 21\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-21\">[21]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>The “wings” are spring-loaded, which allows them to fold and extend easily.</li> \n    <li>You can install toggle bolts in hollow-core concrete, drywall, or plaster.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Hang-Pictures&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Securing the Pictures in Place\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Securing-the-Pictures-in-Place\">Securing the Pictures in Place</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Measure the distance between the hanging hardware and the top of the frame. Look for any hardware attached to the back of your picture, like a D-ring or other type of hook. Place 1 end of your tape measure along this ring or hook, then extend it to the top edge of the picture frame. Commit these measurements to memory, or jot them down on a separate piece of paper so you don’t forget them.<sup id=\"_ref-22\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 22\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-22\">[22]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-15-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 15 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/90/Hang-Pictures-Step-15-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-15-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re measuring lots of pictures at once, it may help to jot everything down on a sticky note.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Mark these measurements on the wall. Find the original markings that you made when you were arranging the templates. Align the top of the tape measure with this mark, and mark off the distance between the top of the frame and the hanging hardware. Repeat this process for any other pictures you plan on hanging up so they can look as centered as possible!<sup id=\"_ref-23\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 23\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-23\">[23]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-16-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 16 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3a/Hang-Pictures-Step-16-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-16-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Double-check your measurements if you’re using 2 pieces of hanging hardware. Stick a long strip of painter’s tape along the top edge of a level, so you can record measurements on the tape. Place this level directly beneath any hanging hardware attached to the back of the frame. Mark on the painter’s tape where each piece of hanging hardware goes. Then, hold the balanced level along the wall and transfer those pencil marks there, so you know where the hardware needs to go.<sup id=\"_ref-24\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 24\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-24\">[24]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-17-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 17 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/01/Hang-Pictures-Step-17-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-17-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re only using 1 piece of hanging hardware with your picture, you can disregard this.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Drill a pilot hole if the hardware requires it. Note that certain types of hardware, like D-rings and toggle bolts, need to be mounted directly into the wall. If you’re working with drywall, place down a strip of painter’s tape, then drill into the designated spot.<sup id=\"_ref-25\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 25\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-25\">[25]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-18-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 18 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0c/Hang-Pictures-Step-18-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-18-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Since painter’s tape is designed for home improvement projects, it won’t damage your walls.<sup id=\"_ref-26\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 26\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-26\">[26]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>Stick a folded sticky note on your wall before drilling any pilot holes. This will help catch any dust and leftover residue.<sup id=\"_ref-27\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 27\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-27\">[27]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Install your hanging hardware of choice into the wall. Screw or insert your hardware into the hole so your picture is supported. Repeat this process with however many pictures you plan on hanging up, so all of your decor will be ready to display.<sup id=\"_ref-28\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 28\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-28\">[28]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-19-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 19 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c7/Hang-Pictures-Step-19-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-19-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For instance, if you’re using D-rings, you’ll need to screw anchors into the wall. These will come packaged with the actual D-rings.<sup id=\"_ref-29\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 29\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-29\">[29]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>If you’re using adhesive hanging strips, you won’t need to install any extra hardware. Regardless, you may want to stick the strips to the wall before hanging up your picture.<sup id=\"_ref-30\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 30\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-30\">[30]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Place felt or rubber bumpers along the back corners of the picture. Arrange adhesive felt or rubber bumpers on the 4 corners along the backside of your art, which will prevent your decor from scratching the wall. At this point, you’re ready to display and admire your beautiful pictures!<sup id=\"_ref-31\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 31\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-31\">[31]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-20-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 20 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e9/Hang-Pictures-Step-20-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-20-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Hang your pictures using the proper hardware. Line up each picture in front of its respective hardware, whether it’s a D-ring, toggle bolt, or self-tapping anchor. Double-check that your picture is lined up with any hardware on the wall before mounting it. Take a step back to make sure your picture is centered. If your picture isn’t centered, adjust it as necessary so you can admire your beautiful art!<sup id=\"_ref-32\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 32\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-32\">[32]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Hang-Pictures-Step-21-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Hang Pictures Step 21 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/30/Hang-Pictures-Step-21-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-21-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can hang up D-rings by lining the rings up with the hooks you installed in the wall.</li> \n    <li>Mount your picture on the hook that’s threaded to your toggle bolt.</li> \n    <li>Place your picture over the hook if you used a self-tapping anchor.<sup id=\"_ref-33\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 33\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-33\">[33]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>If you’re using adhesive hanging strips, check that your picture is firmly stuck to the wall.<sup id=\"_ref-34\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 34\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-34\">[34]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Hang-Pictures&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Screw metal brackets onto the back corners of your pictures to give them extra support.<sup id=\"_ref-35\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 35\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-35\">[35]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>For extra security, you can thread a long piece of hanging wire through the D-rings attached to your picture frame. Loop the wire through the rings, then twist it around itself so the wire stays taut. You can now use this wire to display your picture!<sup id=\"_ref-36\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 36\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-36\">[36]</a></sup></li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Hang-Pictures&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Avoid hanging pictures with just 1 nail. In many cases, a single nail won’t provide enough support for your picture.<sup id=\"_ref-37\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 37\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Hang-Pictures#_note-37\">[37]</a></sup></li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Hang-Pictures&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Things You’ll Need\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Things-You’ll-Need\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Things-You.E2.80.99ll-Need\">Things You’ll Need</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Craft paper or newspaper</li> \n  <li>Painter’s tape</li> \n  <li>Pencil</li> \n  <li>Tape measure</li> \n  <li>Level</li> \n  <li>Thumbtack</li> \n  <li>Stud finder</li> \n  <li>Hanging hardware</li> \n  <li>Electric drill</li> \n  <li>Rubber bumpers</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Hang-Pictures&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: References\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span /Hang-Pictures-Step-16-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-16-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn56@2020_5/2020/10/18/17-02-17-293_18da485f5d781173.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/01/Hang-Pictures-Step-17-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-17-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn95@2020_4/2020/10/18/17-02-17-164_16d02f15dfe84947.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0c/Hang-Pictures-Step-18-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-18-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn39@2020_2/2020/10/18/17-02-17-150_c50aa02bfd9ad543.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c7/Hang-Pictures-Step-19-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-19-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn3@2020_5/2020/10/18/17-02-17-081_b7eec2fa05101630.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e9/Hang-Pictures-Step-20-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-20-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn91@2020_3/2020/10/18/17-02-16-188_b250d7d7f228aaa6.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/30/Hang-Pictures-Step-21-Version-2.jpg/aid1322002-v4-728px-Hang-Pictures-Step-21-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn15@2020_2/2020/10/18/17-02-17-606_bb80059ac7023974.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603040522127},{"createdTime":"2020-10-19 01:02:02","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 01:02:02","title":"How to Do a Tabata Workout at Home","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>If you follow different fitness trends, you may be familiar with Tabata, a vigorous type of High Intensity Interval Training (HIIT) that you can do within a few minutes. Unlike regular HIIT exercise, Tabata follows an especially strict formula of exercising and resting, which allows you to build endurance and burn fat more easily.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup> You can include a variety of cardio and strength exercises into your routine, depending on what your workout goals are. If you’re looking for a quick but efficient workout, Tabata may be a good solution for your fitness needs. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Tabata Basics\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tabata-Basics\">Tabata Basics</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Stretch out to warm up your body before you exercise. Focus on stretching out all parts of your body, like your neck, shoulders, and legs. After stretching on your own, ask a friend or family member if they’d be willing to do some partner stretches with you. Give yourself several minutes to warm up so you aren’t at risk of spraining or pulling a muscle.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-01.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 01.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c1/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-01.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-01.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For instance, you can do some neck rolls to stretch out your neck, then move onto forward, backward, left, and right arm swings.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Exercise vigorously for 20 seconds. Set a timer for 20 seconds and start performing the exercise of your choice. Do your best to push yourself to the absolute limit as you work, even if it’s uncomfortable.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup> If you’re having trouble keeping track of your workout time, use a Tabata timer to help.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-02.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 02.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/dc/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-02.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-02.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>These exercises can be anything that get your blood pumping, like jumping jacks, crunches, sprints, and more. You can focus on just cardio or strength training, or choose activities that cover both categories.</li> \n    <li>You can find a Tabata timer here: <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://www.uwgb.edu/university-recreation/online-resources/tabata-workouts\">https://www.uwgb.edu/university-recreation/online-resources/tabata-workouts</a>.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Let yourself rest for 10 seconds. Slow down or pause after your intense workout, giving yourself a brief period to catch your breath.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup> If needed, use a Tabata timer to help you keep track of how long you rest for, so you don’t mess up the flow of your workout.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-03.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 03.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b7/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-03.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-03.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>As tempting as it is to give yourself extra rest time, try to limit yourself to just 10 seconds. It’ll feel really exhausting at the time, but these exercises will help you build endurance!</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Alternate exercise and rest until you’ve worked out for 4 minutes. Continue exercising for 20 seconds, working as hard as you physically can. Break for 10 seconds, then repeat the cycle all over again. After 4 minutes, you can stop.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-04.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 04.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/7d/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-04.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-04.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Some people prefer to do several 4-minute Tabata circuits, giving themselves 1 minute of rest in between each segment.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cool down for several minutes once you’ve finished working out. Start by walking in place, rotating your arms in circles as you go. Transition into a calf stretch, then switch to a hamstring stretch. At this point, pull up each leg towards your glutes for a dynamic quad stretch. Once you’ve done this, extend your arms behind you to stretch your chest, and pull them forward to stretch your back. Finish off with some tricep stretches, along with side stretches that engage your side muscles.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-05.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 05.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6b/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-05.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-05.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Always take time to cool down and stretch, even if it’s only for a few minutes. This will help prevent strain or injury in the long run!</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Limit yourself to 2 Tabata sessions each week. Plan out your exercise goals for the week. While Tabata is a great workout, don’t expect to be doing it every day. Instead, limit yourself to 2 days each week, supplementing the rest of your time with other workouts and exercises.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-06.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 06.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/20/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-06.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-06.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For instance, you can go for a bike ride on Monday; do Tabata on Tuesday; go for a swim on Wednesday: do more Tabata on Thursday; and go for a run on Friday.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Choosing Exercises for Tabata\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Choosing-Exercises-for-Tabata\">Choosing Exercises for Tabata</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Get your heart pumping with sprints and walking lunges. Find an open area in your home where you can safely run in place without crashing into or colliding with anything. Run in place as fast as you can for 20 seconds, then transition into walking lunges for 10 seconds to slow yourself down.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-07.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 07.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/93/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-07.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-07.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>To perform a walking lunge, step forward, bending 1 knee in front and 1 behind you. Take a “step” forward, lunging forward with your opposite leg while leaving the other bent behind you.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Incorporate narrow and wide squats into your Tabata routine. Lay out a yoga mat to cushion your feet, leaving your feet together. Take a squat, bending your knees at a 90-degree angle. Lift yourself from this position and jump, spreading your feet apart as you land. Squat down, then straighten up and bring your feet together. Repeat these alternating squats for 20 seconds as part of your Tabata workout!<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-08.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 08.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/08/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-08.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-08.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Try to switch between these squats as rapidly as possible to get the full effect.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Grab a chair and do some step-ups. Pull over a sturdy chair next to you in your workout space. Pretend that you’re climbing a staircase by stepping onto the seat of the chair with both feet, then stepping back down onto the floor. Repeat this stepping movement as quickly as you can for 20 seconds.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-09.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 09.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/26/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-09.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-09.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Double-check that the chair is sturdy, and that you can comfortably climb on it without any difficulty.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Lean against a wall to do an easy wall sit. Find an open wall in your home that doesn’t have any decorations. Plant your feet firmly on the ground, keeping your back flush against the wall. Bend your knees at a 90-degree angle, holding this “seated” squat for 20 seconds.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/74/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-10.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Strengthen your abs with some crunches. Find a comfortable place where you can lay down in your home, or roll out a yoga mat. Lay face-up on the mat and perform as many crunches as you can for 20 seconds.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/01/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-11.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>As uncomfortable as it may feel, do your best to push yourself to limit as you exercise.</li> \n    <li>As an example Tabata workout, you can cycle between crunches, lunges, burpees, and planks.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Try a regular or reverse plank to engage your core. Find an open, comfortable area where you can stretch out along the floor. Hold a basic plank position on your forearms for 20 seconds, or try a reverse plank, where you balance yourself on your palms while keeping your legs and chest at a rigid, 45-degree angle.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e0/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-12.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>With reverse planks, only your heels will be on the ground.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Get some cardio in with butt-kicks or high-knees. Run in place as fast as you can. Do some high-knees by lifting your legs higher in the air while you run. You can also try some butt-kicks, where you bring your heel to your glutes as you move. Continue either of these exercises for 20 seconds as part of your Tabata workout.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/df/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-13.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Always make sure you’re running in an open area where you aren’t at risk of colliding with anything around you.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Push yourself to the limit with burpees. Roll out a yoga mat so your body is supported and cushioned while you exercise. Get down in a push-up position, then jump onto your feet. Jump into the air and return to the original push-up position, repeating this exercise for 20 seconds.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-14.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 14.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d7/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-14.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-14.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Using At-Home Equipment\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Using-At-Home-Equipment\">Using At-Home Equipment</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Add a kettlebell into your normal Tabata workout. Try some exercises that involve holding, swinging, or lifting a kettlebell. Start by bending your knees and swinging the piece of equipment down through your legs. Then, using your hips as momentum, swing the kettlebell upwards and bring it up to your shoulder height. Bring the kettlebell back between your legs and bend your knees to repeat the exercise for 20 seconds.<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-15.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 15.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6a/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-15.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-15.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can find kettlebells online, or at most stores that sell fitness equipment.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Include jump ropes in your circuit for a good workout. Jump rope for 20 seconds, trying a “double under” technique to really get your blood pumping. Try to swing the rope beneath yourself twice before your feet hit the ground, which provides an especially tough workout. Above all else, focus on jumping rope as quickly as you can.<sup id=\"_ref-19\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 19\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-19\">[19]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-16.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 16.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c1/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-16.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-16.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Work out with a rowing machine to get vigorous exercise. Visit your local or home gym and find the rowing machine, which gives you a good full-body workout. Set your rowing machine to a high weight setting and do as many reps as you can in 20 seconds.<sup id=\"_ref-20\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 20\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-20\">[20]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-17.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 17.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0a/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-17.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-17.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Intense rowing workouts usually involve 28 “strokes,” or reps, per minute.</li> \n    <li>During your rest period, don’t stop completely—just relax a bit on the machine.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Do a cardio-centric Tabata workout with your treadmill or bike. Set your treadmill to a speed where you’ll be completely sprinting. Maintain this speed for 20 seconds, then slow it down for 10 seconds. Repeat these adjustments as you continue your Tabata workout.<sup id=\"_ref-21\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 21\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-21\">[21]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-18.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Do a Tabata Workout at Home Step 18.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c0/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-18.jpg/aid12069556-v4-728px-Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home-Step-18.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can also perform this exercise without a treadmill—you’ll just have to closely monitor your speed.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <p><br /> </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Follow workout videos or programs if you’d like a little extra guidance as you exercise.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Talk to your doctor before trying Tabata if you have a severe health issue, like a heart condition. Your doctor may offer advice, suggestions, and alternatives that can help you stay safe while you exercise.<sup id=\"_ref-22\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 22\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Do-a-Tabata-Workout-at-Home#_note-22\">[22]</a></sup></li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span
